  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_de9f9472-dade-44c1-8804-2683a41338bd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText7654275665676888177" style="display:none">ENEMIES DON’T NEED TO BE ALIVE TO BE DEADLY.<br /> <br />For Chess Putnam, finding herself near-fatally poisoned by a con psychic and then stopping a murderous ghost is just another day on the job. As an agent of the Church of Real Truth, Chess must expose those looking to profit from the world’s unpleasant little poltergeist problem—humans filing false claims of hauntings—all while staving off any undead who really are looking for a kill. But Chess has been extra busy these days, coping with a new “celebrity” assignment while trying on her own time to help some desperate prostitutes.<br /><br />Someone’s taking out the hookers of Downside in the most gruesome way, and Chess is sure the rumors that it’s the work of a ghost are way off base. But proving herself right means walking in the path of a maniac, not to mention standing between the two men in her life just as they—along with their ruthless employers—are moving closer to a catastrophic showdown. Someone is dealing in murder, sex, and the supernatural, and once again Chess finds herself right in the crossfire.</span>

<div id="review_205370312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205370312" />
    <a title="Dija" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2857113-dija"><img alt="Dija" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360335537p2/2857113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205370312?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dija" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dija" href="/user/show/2857113-dija">Dija</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=surprisingly-good">surprisingly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=uf-or-pnr">uf-or-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2857113-dija?shelf=buddy-slash-group-read">buddy-slash-group-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205370312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8426774174149545558"><b>Thoughts before reading:</b><br/><br/>I'm going to give this series one more chance, for this and this alone:<br/><blockquote><i>“Readers have the right to say whatever the fuck they want about a book. Period. They have that right. If they hate the book because the MC says the word “delicious” and the reader believes it’s the Devil’s word and only evil people use it, they can shout from the rooftops “This book is shit and don’t read it” if they want. If they want to write a review entirely about how much they hate the cover, the</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8426774174149545558" style="display:none"><b>Thoughts before reading:</b><br /><br />I'm going to give this series one more chance, for this and this alone:<br /><blockquote><i>“Readers have the right to say whatever the fuck they want about a book. Period. They have that right. If they hate the book because the MC says the word “delicious” and the reader believes it’s the Devil’s word and only evil people use it, they can shout from the rooftops “This book is shit and don’t read it” if they want. If they want to write a review entirely about how much they hate the cover, they can if they want. If they want to make their review all about how their dog Foot Foot especially loved to pee on that particular book, they can.” </i> - Stacia Kane</blockquote><br /><s>Okay, fine, there's Terrible love mixed up in there as well, but it's <i>mostly</i> because of the above-mentioned quote.</s><br /><br /><b>Thoughts after reading:</b><br /><br />I've never wanted to love a series as much as I wanted to love Downside Ghosts. I didn't like the first book in the series at all, and I'd dropped DG because I was convinced it simply wasn't for me, but with the recent (or not-so-recent, come to think of it) authors versus reviewers drama going around and more specifically, Kane's admirable stand on it, I was determined to like her series. <br /><br />For the first half of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6557156.Unholy_Magic__Downside_Ghosts___2_" title="Unholy Magic (Downside Ghosts, #2) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Magic</a>, I was positive I'd hate it like I did <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>. But slowly, I began understanding the plot, slang, and Chess which led to a noticeable difference in my enjoyment of the book. <br /><br />I don't love this series yet, but I like the writing and story enough to be excited about reading on. Chess is still a wild card, but I'm looking forward to getting to know her better.<br /><br />3.5/5 stars<br /><br /><b>For more reviews, visit my <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8426774174149545558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="HeatherJay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5969410-heatherjay"><img alt="HeatherJay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529554632p2/5969410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254436430?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HeatherJay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HeatherJay" href="/user/show/5969410-heatherjay">HeatherJay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5969410-heatherjay?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5969410-heatherjay?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254436430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3874353709680235959">I now have a seemingly unhealthy crush on a fictional character with protruding eyebrows, scars on his face, pomade in his hair and mutton chops that would make any Elvis impersonater weak with envy.<br/><br/>I originally started this series right after I finished reading the Fever series.I was in a bit of a Jericho Barrons detox phase that resulted in a lot of good books being tossed aside. Luckily, I picked these up again and can say it is one of may favorite series that I have read. Chess has grown on </span>
  <span id="freeText3874353709680235959" style="display:none">I now have a seemingly unhealthy crush on a fictional character with protruding eyebrows, scars on his face, pomade in his hair and mutton chops that would make any Elvis impersonater weak with envy.<br /><br />I originally started this series right after I finished reading the Fever series.I was in a bit of a Jericho Barrons detox phase that resulted in a lot of good books being tossed aside. Luckily, I picked these up again and can say it is one of may favorite series that I have read. Chess has grown on me. In the beginning, her decisions annoyed me as ridiculously self-destructive and shallow. In Unholy Magic, parts of her past are revealed that explain her actions and why she deals with things the way that she does. She has two very different men in her life. Lex, who supplies her with drugs and a shallow "relationship" based on sex and drugs that creates an environment that helps her forget her past, temporarily, and doesn't ask anything of her emotionally. Then there is Terrible *swoon* (see above). Terrible treats her with respect and dignity and loves her for who she is, warts and all, which seems to be more than she is ready to handle. What transpires between these two during this book is heart-breaking. I never thought anyone would come close to how perfect Barrons is but Terrible gives him a run for his money. If given the opportunity I would stalk him until he had nowhere else to hide and then make him mine.<br /><br />Stacia Kane has created a wonderfully dark and gritty world that I find fascinating and unique. I've already started the next one. Let's hope Chess can get her shit together long enough to fix what transpired in this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3874353709680235959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_353291650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353291650" />
    <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog"><img alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353291650?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-favorite">why-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-favorite-author">why-favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-not-mm">what-not-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-modern-fantasy">what-modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-author-rocks">why-author-rocks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-favorite-series">why-favorite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353291650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5059702810831236319">Update 7/19/12: Stacia Kane is extremely cool:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.staciakane.net/2012/07/11/avengingwtfery/'>http://www.staciakane.net/2012/07/11/...</a><br/>_____________________________<br/><br/><br/>This book hurts. Well, if that lovey dovey stuff matters to you it might. It's not romance at all, it's painful and raw and sick but I cried. I didn't even know I was crying until my lip felt wet.<br/><br/>I also couldn't put it down. I started trying to read around eleven but the kids kept interrupting until after twelve when I was already exhausted. By two I was having trouble keeping my ey</span>
  <span id="freeText5059702810831236319" style="display:none">Update 7/19/12: Stacia Kane is extremely cool:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.staciakane.net/2012/07/11/avengingwtfery/">http://www.staciakane.net/2012/07/11/...</a><br />_____________________________<br /><br /><br />This book hurts. Well, if that lovey dovey stuff matters to you it might. It's not romance at all, it's painful and raw and sick but I cried. I didn't even know I was crying until my lip felt wet.<br /><br />I also couldn't put it down. I started trying to read around eleven but the kids kept interrupting until after twelve when I was already exhausted. By two I was having trouble keeping my eyes open but something was about to happen with Terrible so I had to keep going. I got some caffeine and read further. Soon I had to pee. I sat with my legs crossed until five and when I couldn't hold it any longer. By then I was almost done with the book even though I had reread almost every scene with the two of them. I finally finished at 6 AM when I had to get up at 11AM. That's how good this book was. <br /><br />Why? I'm not entirely sure. The premise is ridiculous. Even if you bought the idea of the cataclysmic event, the author knows little about religion and systems of belief and how they endure and adapt to changing times; changes like modern tragedies, technological inventions, astronomical developments (round earth, space travel), and those that refuse to change despite overwhelming evidence (Flat Earth Society, Intelligent Design). It would take a lot longer for this new absurd religion to take hold and much longer for the others to lose complete faith. Elders coming back from the dead to murder most of your family would only convince those who worship elders that they weren't doing a good enough job. And how would they have found the city of the dead and not be killed? And if the dead were so evil why are people not afraid of the city of the dead? It's really quite confusing. <br /><br />But ignore that foundation that was set in the first book. Ignore the occasional poorly constructed or pronoun laden sentence that has to be reread to be understood. Ignore it because most of the writing is good enough that I usually didn't notice it and I could almost always picture the scene like it was a movie in my head. I could see every move Terrible made; every flippant expression on Lex's face, the battles and the ghosts and the blood. The drug withdrawal scene was so well done I started to become nauseated. I ached for that person but I liked that the person was having consequences of being an addict and hope that this continues to be an increasing theme. I like that we never really see Chess's love interests use (except for a life saving emergency in the first book) even when she is with them when she pops a few pills.<br /><br />The plot moves along at a good clip and the mysteries are just that and it isn't until near the big finale that you finally figure it all out. <br /><br />But what I love best are the people. These are the best characters I think I have ever read in Urban Fantasy. They are damaged people and they do bad things but I don't believe the author glorifies them. I think she just presents them as they are and forces the reader to read between the lines. I think this was true in the first book too. Chess has to have her fix and she is always worried about how she is going to cope with what she's taken or whether/what she needs to get through. She admits she's an addict but her life is so low to her that she doesn't care. In this book, she talks several times about how much easier it would be to just let herself be killed because of all the darkness; that it was right that no one respects her or trusts her because she is not worthy of it. It's heart wrenching. <br /><br />Bump and Slobag could be just caricatures but Kane gives them just enough more that they feel real to me. <br /><br />Lex is a bit of an enigma and I hate that Kane keeps having him doing things that make me like him although the not-black-and-white aspect is something I really admire. He's no worse than the others and in some ways better than most because he never lies about what he does. He also doesn't throw his power around or boast about it all the time but he has plenty of faults. I keep waiting for him to hurt Chess but instead he keeps helping her and is there when she needs him. <br /><br />Terrible though is one of the best main characters I have read about in a long time. He is complex and I get the impression there is so much more under the surface, much more than the hidden layers we've already been shown. I love that he's ugly. I love his slang and uneducated speech patterns. I love that he's smarter than he knows. I love that he actually does terrible things and that bothers Chess especially when she sees them and he doesn't want her to see him like that. I love that he has deep feelings that are sometimes obvious to me but are not at all clear to the other characters. I love that he's this kind of tacky pseudo-50's James Dean/Grease cross with a pompadour (ewwww) and drives a muscle car. I love that somehow I know that Terrible doesn't like that Chess does drugs because he worries about her even though he's never said anything, implied or done anything <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[except to say something along the lines of he'll want her no matter what <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to says so. Somehow by omission, Kane has let me figure this out. I know some of these sound like stereotypes but Kane makes it fresh and new. I am in love with Terrible which is quite a kudo to Kane given what a passifist and anti-drug person I am. She's that good. <br /><br />4 stars plus one more for making me read so fast and grabbing my heart like that.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5059702810831236319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240673220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240673220" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240673220?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of urban fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Penny by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now">Wicked Incognito Now</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=grrrl-power">grrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=witchy-woman">witchy-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=penny-s-favorite-books">penny-s-favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240673220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6660334170254503101"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kat</a>, fellow Goodreader (and my favorite Australian) summed up this book best: gut-wrenching. This book ripped out my innards, tap danced all over them, unceremoniously shoved them back inside me, and sewed me up haphazardly. Sure, in the end, my guts were no longer all over the place but serious damage was done. And I liked it. <br/><br/>Sounds like I'm being over-dramatic, I know, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/9574772' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>you should see my Unholy Magic status updates</a>.<br/><br/>This book sent me on an emotional roller coaster ride from hell. Now, don't</span>
  <span id="freeText6660334170254503101" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat</a>, fellow Goodreader (and my favorite Australian) summed up this book best: gut-wrenching. This book ripped out my innards, tap danced all over them, unceremoniously shoved them back inside me, and sewed me up haphazardly. Sure, in the end, my guts were no longer all over the place but serious damage was done. And I liked it. <br /><br />Sounds like I'm being over-dramatic, I know, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/9574772" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">you should see my Unholy Magic status updates</a>.<br /><br />This book sent me on an emotional roller coaster ride from hell. Now, don't get me wrong, this isn't a bad thing. I mean, I do love roller coasters. I love the sensation of plunging down steep slopes and shooting through loop-de-loops at eleventy-billion miles an hour. I love screaming like a maniac, thinking I might die any second (knowing I won't). But see, that's just a regular roller coaster ride.<br /><br />Unholy Magic, is more like a terrifying ride on a rickety old roller coaster that may or may not be missing some track. While being stark naked. Halfway through the ride you see that, indeed, there is a section of the track missing, and you realize you're about to die--But, wait! Instead of flying off the track and plummeting to a gruesome death, the roller coaster sails across the gap--Speed style--and lands on the other side, tracks lined up and everything. It's unbelievable. <br /><br />In the end you're still alive and you feel exhilarated and invincible and you want to do it again. You see that you can because, hey, there aren't many people in line. But as you prepare to get up you vomit in the lap of the stranger sitting next to you. Oh, and hey, you're still mysteriously naked. <br /><br />It's horrible, but in the best way possible. Does that make sense?<br /><br />Now you're probably thinking I don't like this book--I mean, "horrible in the best way possible" doesn't sound like high praise, amirite? Well, you couldn't be more wrong. I enjoyed Unholy Magic despite all the feelings--some downright beautiful, some so cringe-worthy I wanted to crawl in a hole and die--it stirred within me.<br /><br />I don't know, I guess another way to describe the experience is by saying Kane's writing is so good I felt as though I was there, within the pages of the book, watching everything play out. Not only that but I felt all of the characters emotions and it was amazing and terrifying and overwhelming all at the same time.<br /><br />It was great. <br /><br />I'll be reading Unholy Magic again, sooner rather than later, I just need a little time to recover. Four stars. <br /><br />(a copy of this review is posted at <a href="http://pennystuppence.blogspot.com/2011/12/review-unholy-magic-downside-ghosts-2.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6660334170254503101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_799931737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/799931737" />
    <a title="Erica Ravenclaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12099580-erica-ravenclaw"><img alt="Erica Ravenclaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598276462p2/12099580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/799931737?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Ravenclaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Ravenclaw" href="/user/show/12099580-erica-ravenclaw">Erica Ravenclaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8628408-unholy-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12099580-erica-ravenclaw?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<div id="review_272011121" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272011121" />
    <a title="new_user" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user"><img alt="new_user" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351189841p2/1365355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272011121?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="new_user" class="user" itemprop="url" name="new_user" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user">new_user</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1365355-new-user?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272011121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10932670163561458291"><b>I am appeased.</b> <i>Unholy Magic</i> delivers the meat missing from predecessor <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_' title='Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unholy Ghosts</a>
</i> (Downside Ghosts #1). While still imperfect, <i>Magic</i> offers intricate, clever plotting, powerful prose, and most importantly, a healthy serving of character development. <br/><br/><i>Ghosts</i> irritated me because author Stacia Kane romanticizes drug addiction and drug peddlers. Witch-sleuth protagonist Chess Putnam -the significance of whose surname I will discover eventually!- unaccountably escapes addiction's lowest moment</span>
  <span id="freeText10932670163561458291" style="display:none"><b>I am appeased.</b> <i>Unholy Magic</i> delivers the meat missing from predecessor <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>
</i> (Downside Ghosts #1). While still imperfect, <i>Magic</i> offers intricate, clever plotting, powerful prose, and most importantly, a healthy serving of character development. <br /><br /><i>Ghosts</i> irritated me because author Stacia Kane romanticizes drug addiction and drug peddlers. Witch-sleuth protagonist Chess Putnam -the significance of whose surname I will discover eventually!- unaccountably escapes addiction's lowest moments in <i>Ghosts</i>. Drug dealer Lex doesn't exploit her when she's withdrawing; he's a nice guy, like enforcer Terrible, who charms the local kids. Chess is poor, addicted to illicit painkillers long enough to build a tolerance, but we never see the stupors, the tedium, the humiliation. <i>Ghosts</i> was no <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23940.Junky" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Junky</i>
</a>. That wouldn't entertain us-- but why should drug abuse entertain us? Junkies are boring, and they should be. <br /><br /><i>Magic</i> is no <i>Junky</i> either, but Chess finally sees some consequences, and the same selective, careful manipulation of plot that I lamented in <i>Ghosts</i> because we never saw more honest, darker moments pays off a hundredfold in <i>Magic</i>, where every scene, revelation, and detail, tightly paced, impacts later events, both the murder investigation and the characters' inner lives. The latter admittedly interested me more -Kane intends troubled Chess to evolve, and I eat up the emotional peaks and troughs, especially since Kane does not write with sentimental language- but I can't fault her mystery-writing. She seeds clues and red herrings aplenty.<br /><br />Speaking of language, Kane's prose is strong, tight, and so subdued that similes striking because of their fitness fly by unnoticed.<blockquote>His chapped lips stretched and flaked in a gruesome semblance of a smile, like a fat worm crawling across his face, revealing broken, graying teeth.</blockquote> No cliches. Expect a high dialogue to exposition ratio-- some of the best dialogue in urban fantasy. The invented vernacular lends life, realism, and plasticity to the dialogue, and the script read so far from the standard on-the-nose dialogue parroting a character's internal musings, usually delivered to us point by point just prior, that I was shocked, shocked, I say! when I couldn't guess Chess' next line, although her ineffectual stammering did wear on me. <br /><br />All the same, Terrible's lines, so three-dimensional when he's angry--! I have to agree that he carries the book. He's a strong guy.<br /><br />So, I look forward to <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7352840.City_of_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___3_" title="City of Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #3) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Ghosts</a>
</i> and coming books, and I recommend this for any fans of gritty! Four stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10932670163561458291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer830769043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6441005239243040204"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Oh Chess. What a piece of freaking work you are. ::Shakes head::</b> <br/><br/>This series is dark, dark, dark, and more than a little depressing. I'm not usually a fan of downer reads. So why is it so good? How is this series so freaking good? And why can I not stop reading (or listening, in my case)?!?! Chess is a drugged out mess, and only sinking deeper into her own pit of suck. But Stacia Kane is kind of brilliant how she writes her character. Chess was worse than ever but I <i>felt</i> for her for the first ti</span>
  <span id="freeText6441005239243040204" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Oh Chess. What a piece of freaking work you are. ::Shakes head::</b> <br><br>This series is dark, dark, dark, and more than a little depressing. I'm not usually a fan of downer reads. So why is it so good? How is this series so freaking good? And why can I not stop reading (or listening, in my case)?!?! Chess is a drugged out mess, and only sinking deeper into her own pit of suck. But Stacia Kane is kind of brilliant how she writes her character. Chess was worse than ever but I <i>felt</i> for her for the first time. I had empathy, man, empathy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390966505ra/8307509.gif" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The way Bahni Turpin narrates this book makes me want to talk all cool and "downside"-y, which is inadvisable for me, considering I'm a uncool suburban mom. I want to casually drop in a "facts are truth" to someone. This book just gets under your skin. It made me want to visit the world of Downside Ghosts, if only as a casual observer (that place is freaking creepy and scary, dude). <br><br>I want to slap some sense into Chess but I also want to follow her around and witness her brilliance and her coming to pieces. <br><br>I loved this story and I will be listening to the rest of the series back to back. Stacia Kane, go easy on me. <br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775484963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15700999958643879439"><b>
  <i>“Nothin show up we ain’t handle, aye? You an me.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I am officially <b>addicted</b> to this series! This book <b>killed me, but I love, love, loved</b> it! It’s been over a month since I read Unholy Magic for the first time. Since then I have listened to it on audio 1 & ½ more times and also re-read parts of it. It’s <b>
  <i>that freaking good!</i>
</b><br/><br/>What an AMAZING sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478043471' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unholy Ghosts</a>! I don’t think there’s anything about this book that I didn’t like. The plot was really interesting and I enjoyed the parts of Ches</span>
  <span id="freeText15700999958643879439" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Nothin show up we ain’t handle, aye? You an me.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I am officially <b>addicted</b> to this series! This book <b>killed me, but I love, love, loved</b> it! It’s been over a month since I read Unholy Magic for the first time. Since then I have listened to it on audio 1 &amp; ½ more times and also re-read parts of it. It’s <b>
  <i>that freaking good!</i>
</b><br /><br />What an AMAZING sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478043471" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>! I don’t think there’s anything about this book that I didn’t like. The plot was really interesting and I enjoyed the parts of Chess doing her regular Church debunking job even more in this one. She is given the assignment to check out an alleged haunting of celebrity, Roger Pyle’s home. I was kind of fascinated by the dynamic of the Pyle’s. They are so dysfunctional and messed up and the whole time I really couldn’t tell what was genuine. It was fun to actually care about the case and try to figure things out right there alongside Chess. <br /><br />Of course, investigating the Pyle’s haunting isn’t the only thing Chess is doing for work. Always caught in the middle of things, she’s still working for drug dealers Bump (&amp; Terrible) on one side and Slobag (&amp; Lex) on the other. This situation has always put me on edge. With her drug habit and personal relationships with both Terrible and Lex… Ughhh… I want to slap Chess sometimes. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>And sometime soon—shit, she hadn’t even asked when—she’d be standing around with all of them. Bump and Slobag, Terrible and Lex. Every one of whom thought she owed them something. Not to mention her mysterious friend, the one who’d left human body parts in her car outside her work and followed her through the dark streets. How the fuck had she gotten herself into this one. Did she want to be killed?</blockquote>
</i><br />A lot and I mean A LOT happens in terms of the relationships in this book. Chess is still having her no strings attached thing with Lex, but we all know there’s no feelings there. But her friendship or whatever it is with Terrible is what gets to me. We all know they want each other! It just lingers there and it’s brutal!<br /><i>
  <blockquote>Like playing with forbidden spells early in her training, like the rush of a line of speed she wanted just a little too much, she wanted this. Wanted to take from him and give back, too. Wanted to share something. </blockquote>
</i><br />Chess and Terrible have their first real argument in this book. Followed by Terrible proving <i>once again</i> how much he cares and how loyal he is. Then comes the kicker, he lays out in front of Chess and all she has to do it grab it. Good god, that speech. Terrible… Oh my god, I don’t think I could possibly love him any more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
    <i>“Shit. I want you, Chess. Make no mistake on that one, dig? Want you bad. So bad I ain’t even can think of any else sometimes, ’cept gettin you under me. Ain’t give a fuck what pills you swallow get you through the day or what happens you ain’t got em, aye? Still want you.”<br /><br />“But I ain’t … ain’t think I can take it, wakin up next to you on the morn, have you fake like nothin happened. Or tell me you made yourself a mistake. Or say, aye, thanks, maybe try that again on the sometime. I know how you run it, keepin it cool and no repeats, and I dig it, aye? Got your reasons. So I figure…”<br /><br />“I figure you really wanted me you’d say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I’ll fuckin carry you down your place on a run, you tell me aye, get you on your back afore the next word comes out your mouth. But you oughta have yourself certain, causen I ain’t lookin for charity, an I ain’t lettin you go after. Once … once ain’t enough for me, dig?”</i>
  </blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And here is another moment that I wanted to smack Chess…<br /><i>
  <blockquote>Her mouth refused to open, to utter that one small word that was all he needed to hear. Her body was taking its revenge on her, and what a time it picked.</blockquote>
</i><br />As much as it might sound like I don’t like Chess, I really do. I love her. She’s an awesome narrator and such a complex character. I don’t know how she does it, but even when she’s messing up or making HUGE mistakes, I feel for her the whole time. I know she really means well and to hear how she owns and can admit to her downfalls and flaws is truly heartbreaking at times. <br /><br />This installment is full of heartache and emotion (and the action is still definitely there, too). Everything comes to a head and it’s incredibly intense. Every time I thought the worst had come, I felt like I was punched in the gut once again. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i> “How long, Chess?”</i> *SOB* and <i>“Naw,” he said. “Naw, Chess, you ain’t a whore. A whore’s honest.”</i> *DAGGER TO THE HEART* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was sobbing through more than one part of this book. It completely exceeded by expectations and I am dying to jump into the next book. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>She wasn’t scared anymore. Being with him wouldn’t be scary. Being without him, being alone again … That made her booze-diluted blood run cold.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><i>See more reviews at <a href="http://nobsbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">No BS Book Reviews</a>. <br />Also 'like' us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/NoBsBookReviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</i> ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="15700999958643879439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110949607" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110949607" />
    <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer"><img alt="Carolyn  Storer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457826767p2/2449271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110949607?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn  Storer" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer">Carolyn  Storer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007343256" href="/book/show/7553216-unholy-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=book-list-2010">book-list-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110949607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14175245466893998177">After reading and absolutely loving Unholy Ghosts, I was somewhat nervous about reading Unholy Magic. I've been caught out before with a new series, reading and liking the first book only to be disappointed with the second, but thankfully, this was not the case with Unholy Magic. This book is AMAZING and I am totally in love with this series!<br/><br/>Unholy Magic begins roughly where Unholy Ghosts ended. Chess is still working for the Church of Real Truth as a debunker and popping pills, Terrible is stil</span>
  <span id="freeText14175245466893998177" style="display:none">After reading and absolutely loving Unholy Ghosts, I was somewhat nervous about reading Unholy Magic. I've been caught out before with a new series, reading and liking the first book only to be disappointed with the second, but thankfully, this was not the case with Unholy Magic. This book is AMAZING and I am totally in love with this series!<br /><br />Unholy Magic begins roughly where Unholy Ghosts ended. Chess is still working for the Church of Real Truth as a debunker and popping pills, Terrible is still Bumps enforcer and Lex is Chess' new drug of choice.<br /><br />To me this book is very character driven, which is one of the reasons I love it so much - you may have noticed that my reviews are character driven too - if I don't like the characters then it doesn't matter whether the plot is good or not, I just won't be able to connect with the book. But I didn't have that problem with Unholy Magic. It has two of the best characters I've read in the urban fantasy genre; Chess and Terrible. However, although this book is very much about the characters there is also an engaging storyline.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading about the world Kane has created. Downside is very gritty and dark, where drug dealers and gangs rule, prostitutes and pimps sell you their business and ghosts kill. The ghosts in Downside are scary, evil entities and it's Chess' job as a debunker for the Church of Real Truth to make sure that any claims of ghost sightings or hauntings are legitimate. One such case is given to her by an Elder of the Church for a celebrity who claims there's two ghosts in his house. This part of the story, although secondary to the relationships between the characters, is really enjoyable and we get to see Chess fighting ghosts and banishing them, and using her witchy magic.<br /><br />In Unholy Ghosts, Chess unwillingly helped Lex with a problem he had and because of this she is now getting most of her drugs for free, which enables her to pop as many pills as she likes, and we see her falling into her addiction even further. The thing with Chess is that she enjoys them. She likes blocking out the harsh side of her life, the memories of her past filled with physical and mental abuse, and losing herself in the freedom the pills give her. Chess understands what is happening but doesn't really want to face her addiction and although she is fairly strong and brave in her job as a debunker, in life not so much. If something doesn't go to plan or if she feels letdown by someone then she leans on her drugs - uses them as a replacement for people. However, even though Chess is a drug addict it doesn't prevent her from doing her job - most of the time.<br /><br />I heart Chess so much - she is flawed and vulnerable and that's what I love about her, but I can also see strength and determination. She cares about people and desperately wants to help them, even if it's at the risk of her own life. I have a feeling we are going to see Chess grow enormously in future books, there's so much scope for her character and I can't wait to find out how she evolves.<br /><br />We also learn more about Terrible, which shows him in a softer light and makes him even more loveable. Terrible is so endearing he melts my heart, even though I know he has no qualms about killing someone with his bare hands - I know this and Chess knows this, but somehow it just doesn't matter. Terrible reveals quite a bit about his feelings in this instalment. There's a scene between Chess and Terrible that had my heart pounding in my chest, I just couldn't read the pages fast enough to find out what happened next. I won't go any further but let me just say it's heart-wrenching romance at its best.<br /><br />Lex is still very much in the picture, although he does take a bit of a back-seat to the growing dynamics between Chess and Terrible. But he's growing on me. I'm still not convinced he's trustworthy, but I like him.<br /><br />I'm also impressed by the street-speak, or as Kane puts it, "Down-speech". I think it takes a very talented writer to pull-off accents, but Kane does just that. It's different to anything I've read before but it gives the gangs of Downside a very distinctive and original flare.<br /><br />VERDICT:<br /><br />For me, Unholy Magic has the precise combination and balance of everything I love about the urban fantasy genre: action, romance, complex but likeable characters and world building. I adored this book so much from beginning to end - just perfect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14175245466893998177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1192678548" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192678548" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192678548?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=paranormal-ghosts">paranormal-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-witches-and-wizards">fantasy-witches-and-wizards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192678548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2878597455749852036">This is the second book of Chess Putnam's messed up adventures. She's a witch who officially works for the Church (they're in charge of everything since ghosts tried to take over the world and kill everybody). Unofficially, she sometimes does magic for two rival druglords/pimps named Bump and Slobag. Separately; they aren't supposed to know she's working for the other. Life is tricky. It doesn't help when you're a raging drug addict. Chess needs her pills, her powder, her smoke, and whatever els</span>
  <span id="freeText2878597455749852036" style="display:none">This is the second book of Chess Putnam's messed up adventures. She's a witch who officially works for the Church (they're in charge of everything since ghosts tried to take over the world and kill everybody). Unofficially, she sometimes does magic for two rival druglords/pimps named Bump and Slobag. Separately; they aren't supposed to know she's working for the other. Life is tricky. It doesn't help when you're a raging drug addict. Chess needs her pills, her powder, her smoke, and whatever else she can get her hands on. To complicate matters even more, she's kind of seeing Slobag's son, Lex, while secretly pining over Bump's right-hand man, Terrible. But there's no juvenile angst to be found here. The romantic aspects in this series are gritty and prickly, not happy and shiny. <br><br><b>
  <i>Chess and Terrible:</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424981254i/13826879.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's <u>
  <b>a lot</b>
</u>going on in this book. Chess is trying to solve a case for the Church involving a famous actor and his family. She's trying to figure out who is killing Bump's and Slobag's prostitutes. She's juggling her personal life, dealing with addiction...<br><br>I love Chess. She's not your typical protagonist, but there's just something I get about her. She's had a shitty life and has always been treated like crap, so she thinks she deserves it. She has low self-esteem. She's just floundering through life, barely keeping it together. I can't help but cheer for her and be drawn to her story.<br><br>If you're looking for a fast-paced, action-packed series, this isn't it. There are definitely some intense scenes, but sometimes the pacing is SO slow. Usually, that bothers me, but this works. It isn't something I know I'll tear through in 24 hours, but that's ok. <br><br>One last thing. TERRIBLE. I love him!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! A lot happens involving him in this book. I can't wait to read the next one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424981254i/13826880.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2878597455749852036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_262824175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262824175" />
    <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer"><img alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455829739p2/2278800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262824175?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the first book (don't expect something different)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=a-bit-of-mush">a-bit-of-mush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=zzzzzzz">zzzzzzz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=to-the-mystery-machine">to-the-mystery-machine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=suburban-fantasy">suburban-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fucking-love-triangles">fucking-love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=big-fucking-nope">big-fucking-nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=facepalm">facepalm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262824175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8156915650140114537">  <br/><b>
  <u> Things I hate about Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br/>- Chess’ attitude;<br/>- Chess’ drug addiction;<br/>- Chess’ way of handling her problems;<br/>- Terrible’s vocabulary (it messes with my head a lot);<br/>- No likeable characters;<br/>- The love triangle.<br/><br/><b>
  <u> Things I’m neutral about regarding Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br/>- The ghost theme.<br/><br/><b>
  <u> Things I love about Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br/>[empty]<br/><br/><br/>So I guess that sums it up. I said that I’ll give the second book a try (since I hated the first) because <i>Downside Ghosts</i> is such a popular series. I really w</span>
  <span id="freeText8156915650140114537" style="display:none">  <br /><b>
  <u> Things I hate about Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br />- Chess’ attitude;<br />- Chess’ drug addiction;<br />- Chess’ way of handling her problems;<br />- Terrible’s vocabulary (it messes with my head a lot);<br />- No likeable characters;<br />- The love triangle.<br /><br /><b>
  <u> Things I’m neutral about regarding Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br />- The ghost theme.<br /><br /><b>
  <u> Things I love about Downside Ghosts</u>
</b><br />[empty]<br /><br /><br />So I guess that sums it up. I said that I’ll give the second book a try (since I hated the first) because <i>Downside Ghosts</i> is such a popular series. I really want to know why. Am I missing something here?<br /><br />Ok fine, I tried the second book so that I would be fair and guess what? I still don’t like it and I couldn’t even finish it because <b>it’s a waste of time</b>. Don’t blame me. It’s difficult to read a book where you can’t stand the main character. Or any other character. Or the story. Or the universe.<br /><br />So yep, that’s it. I’m finished with the <i> Downside Ghosts</i> series. So long and goodbye!</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2925099970?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Montzalee Wittmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Montzalee Wittmann" href="/user/show/32532051-montzalee-wittmann">Montzalee Wittmann</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2925099970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5121308230465004097">Unholy Magic<br/>Downside Ghosts, Book 2<br/>By: Stacia Kane<br/>Narrated by: Bahni Turpin<br/>This book has a lot more suspense than the first one! My shoulders were so tense by the end of the book I needed a muscle relaxant! This gave a deeper dive into the inner workers of the Church also, especially what they do with the convicted ghosts. In this book she is dealing with someone or something killing prostitutes and making it look like the killer from 20 years ago who is dead. One spotted a ghost. Another case, </span>
  <span id="freeText5121308230465004097" style="display:none">Unholy Magic<br />Downside Ghosts, Book 2<br />By: Stacia Kane<br />Narrated by: Bahni Turpin<br />This book has a lot more suspense than the first one! My shoulders were so tense by the end of the book I needed a muscle relaxant! This gave a deeper dive into the inner workers of the Church also, especially what they do with the convicted ghosts. In this book she is dealing with someone or something killing prostitutes and making it look like the killer from 20 years ago who is dead. One spotted a ghost. Another case, at the same time, is an actor's home and the Church wants to see if they are faking a haunting which is against the law.<br />Chess is having serious problems with her love life which she has brought upon herself. I don't know why either see her. She seems to use drugs more and more too!<br />I like the mysteries, the alternative world that mixes part our world with a different world. Kane is a terrific world builder and uses that to make horror spring to life. It is gritty, full of little hope, no government just The Church that believes in No gods, there are ghosts and magic that is controlled by the Church for good of mankind. (Mostly) Chess works for The Church but they don't know her secret about the drugs. <br />The narration is really, really good! She is perfect for this series!</span>

<div id="review_280991543" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280991543" />
    <a title="Mimi Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4884889-mimi-smith"><img alt="Mimi Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297016674p2/4884889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280991543?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Smith" href="/user/show/4884889-mimi-smith">Mimi Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4884889-mimi-smith?shelf=uf-r">uf-r</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280991543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6112407420439500545"><b>4.25 stars</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"The dead do not offer forgiveness. They do not feel. They do not advance or grow. They remain frozen as they were, save for the replacement of love with hate.<br/>—The Book of Truth, Veraxis, Article 329"</i>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <u>Downside World 201 by Mimi</u>
</b><br/><br/>All right, in addition to the information I got and mentioned in my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_' title='Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unholy Ghosts</a>, here are some other details/facts/questions<br/><br/><b>1)</b>Remember the Church employees that go to the City and do something with ghosts? They're called Liaisers and appar</span>
  <span id="freeText6112407420439500545" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"The dead do not offer forgiveness. They do not feel. They do not advance or grow. They remain frozen as they were, save for the replacement of love with hate.<br />—The Book of Truth, Veraxis, Article 329"</i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <u>Downside World 201 by Mimi</u>
</b><br /><br />All right, in addition to the information I got and mentioned in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>, here are some other details/facts/questions<br /><br /><b>1)</b>Remember the Church employees that go to the City and do something with ghosts? They're called Liaisers and apparently they guide relatives to visit spirits.<br /><br /><i>"The benches along one pale wall were thick with people waiting their turn to be escorted down to the Liaising Rooms, to wait while their assigned Liaiser rode the long train deep into the ground to visit with the pale, emotionless shades of their loved ones or distant ancestors."</i><br /><br /><b>2)</b>Psychopomps seem to be physical beings. Not sure how they're summoned through a skull, but they can be shot and killed-therefore they're alive. They can be birds, too.<br /><br /><b>3)</b>There is such a thing as sex magic. There's death magic, too.<br /><br /><b>4)</b> I'm not sure about this one but I think Haunted Week might be the same as the Week of Terror. Is that when the time became measured as AT, After Truth? Also BT-Before Truth…1924 BT is it measured the same way BC, AD way works? Just when was this Week of Terror happen? Recently or centuries before?<br /><br /><b>5)</b>There are spirit prisoners. Seems like, when you commit an atrocious crime you are punished after death, too.<br /><br /><i>"Punishment of both crime and sin is the exclusive dominion of the Church. That punishment begins before death. Be assured it continues after it.<br />—The Book of Truth, Veraxis, Article 220"</i><br /><br /><b>6)</b> Apparently, most ghosts attack and get violent because it's their nature...<br /><br /><i>"Ghosts … especially murder victims, they just hate. They get stuck in whatever pattern they were in when they died, they don’t evolve or anything.”</i><br /><br /><b>7)</b>You can bind yourself to a ghost/spirit. It's a big offense and there are two ways to do it.<br /><br /><i>"Worse still are those who commit the ultimate evil, who bind themselves unto the dead."<br /><br />"Tyson was a Host, someone who’d made a deal with a spirit to share his body in exchange for power—as opposed to a Bindmate, where the energy was shared but the body kept separate."</i><br /><br />I think the bound ones can be corporal, since one tries to choke Chess. Not sure how that works.<br /><br /><b>8)</b> Every child is tested at 14 to see if it has "talent" for magic. If it does it's taken to the Church and trained.<br /><br />Generally, I have some answers, more questions and I still think all this could've been explained much better.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The story</u>
</b> <br /><br />We first see Chess at work for the Church, at a Seance. She's nearly poisoned but deals with it. I'm not sure why this scene was in the book at all. What is its purpose? I didn't get it.<br /><br />Similarly to the previous book she gets two missions:one for the Church, and one for her drug dealer(s). Her Church one is to discover whether a movie star is faking a sighting. Her other one is to solve murders in Downtown. Some hookers are getting gruesomely killed and Chess senses the presence of sex magic. Pretty soon she gets in a muddle because both drug dealers want her to solve it, but she doesn't want the other to know what she's doing and so on.<br /><br />Her addiction still controls her life, she manages to screw up and still solve the case.<br /><br />The book only started coming together for me at the rooftop. From there on it was I Can't Wait To See What Happens Next. Before? Not so much.<br /> <br /><b>
  <u>Chess&amp;Terrible</u>
</b><br /><br />And just as I <s>knew</s> dreaded, Chess manages to screw things up between them. I think it's the combination of her addiction and some kind of self-destructive quality she has, but it works every time. And her question...<br /><br /><i>"When had being an addict gotten so fucking hard? So exhausting?" </i><br /><br />Oh, Chess. It's not supposed to be easy. You're destroying yourself and maybe even people around you. I liked this observation:<br /><br /><i>"Terrible stood in his usual spot near the back. She headed for him, watching the red lights play off his shiny black hair and illuminate the breathtaking ugliness of his profile. She didn’t notice it anymore, not really; even now her eyes simply slid over it. He was Terrible, that was all. He was her friend … sort of."</i><br /><br />Still, she is in my TFUTL pile(just for her Too Fucked Up To Live). It's not that I'm not sympathetic...I am, but she really, really screws up with Terrible and hurts him. He's effing amazing and she doesn't deserve him. I'll root for them anyway.<br /><br />And the whole Lex thing is stupid. Not a typical Love triangle, but still stupid.<br /><br />Terrible is even better this time around. He's dangerous, strong, vulnerable, gentle, romantic...*sigh*. That rating up there-mostly because of him. I like how he seems old-fashioned and calls girls Dames...he's really great.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Shit. I want you, Chess. Make no mistake on that one, dig? Want you bad. So bad I ain’t even can think of any else sometimes, ’cept gettin you under me. Ain’t give a fuck what pills you swallow get you through the day or what happens you ain’t got em, aye? Still want you.”<br /><br />“I figure you really wanted me you’d say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I’ll fuckin carry you down your place on a run, you tell me aye, get you on your back afore the next word comes out your mouth. But you oughta have yourself certain, causen I ain’t lookin for charity, an I ain’t lettin you go after. Once … once ain’t enough for me, dig?”</i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6112407420439500545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_341116628" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341116628" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476704-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333052331p2/7476704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341116628?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/7476704-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476704-tom?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341116628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6440693337143959286">I’m going with 4.5 on this book of the series just like the first book but for different reasons. This book was so much smoother to read than the first book. With the world building already done in the previous book we are taken right into Chess’s world from the get go. Chess’s drug abuse is still rampant but maybe I’m just a little numb from it because it bothered me less in this book. The main story itself centered more on just two cases and it felt less chaotic that way. Of course that doesn’</span>
  <span id="freeText6440693337143959286" style="display:none">I’m going with 4.5 on this book of the series just like the first book but for different reasons. This book was so much smoother to read than the first book. With the world building already done in the previous book we are taken right into Chess’s world from the get go. Chess’s drug abuse is still rampant but maybe I’m just a little numb from it because it bothered me less in this book. The main story itself centered more on just two cases and it felt less chaotic that way. Of course that doesn’t mean she wasn’t juggling a lot of balls because the story focusses more on her relationships with Terrible and Lex. Anyone that knows me knows that I HATE triangles. Somehow the author pulls this off.<br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ With her relationship with Terrible just developing she seems to keep him at enough of a distance to kind of justify to herself (and me??) that she isn’t leading Terrible on. If she would have committed to Terrible on the roof and then got busted doing Lex I would have been pissed and it would have changed my impression of Chess. Don’t get me wrong I hated how much she hurt Terrible but letting him walk off the roof kinda felt like she wasn’t leading him on. But with like everything in this series Chess does just enough to justify her destructive behavior. Of course I couldn’t believe she ended up at Lex’s but the author does a good job of making you feel like it was just another one of her addictions. Not that it made it right but what is right in Downside?? The whole you don’t know what you have till you lost it rings true and even though she screwed up again you still feel sorry for her somehow. Not as bad as I felt for Terrible of course.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Loving the series even though this book didn’t feel as intense as the first the Chess and Terrible relationship more than made up for it.<br />I will be moving on with the series. (Probably in a half hour…haha)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6440693337143959286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_289337492" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=2_kindle_own">2_kindle_own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289337492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11068248471879544402">If you are looking for a review that discusses this book, keep looking. This one is more of an internal dialog, you know, notes to self. <br/><br/>Self, you have reached the point where you need to examine your relationship with this series. Why? Because you are not a die-hard fan of urban fantasy and this one is pure UF.<br/><br/>Let’s see…you are married to Night Huntress, Dresden Files, and Tales from the Nightside. You are living with Rachael Morgan, Kate Daniels, and the Iron Druid Chronicles. You are dating B</span>
  <span id="freeText11068248471879544402" style="display:none">If you are looking for a review that discusses this book, keep looking. This one is more of an internal dialog, you know, notes to self. <br /><br />Self, you have reached the point where you need to examine your relationship with this series. Why? Because you are not a die-hard fan of urban fantasy and this one is pure UF.<br /><br />Let’s see…you are married to Night Huntress, Dresden Files, and Tales from the Nightside. You are living with Rachael Morgan, Kate Daniels, and the Iron Druid Chronicles. You are dating Black London and Indigo Court. You recently broke up with Black Dagger Brotherhood and happy to see the end of Dark Swan. You are not reliable when you have so many options. You are fickle. Do not lie to yourself.<br /><br />True, you enjoy your time with Chess, Terrible, and the world of Downside but where is this going? One more for the road or are you sated with your experience so far? The series hasn’t let you down but something is making you lace up your running shoes. Could it be that Chess is not even close to getting her shit together? Do you want her to? Is this going to be a ghost thing with no variety? Does Chess have some skill-sets that haven’t manifested yet? What is Terrible now? Exactly how ugly is Terrible? Is Chess going to win his love and devotion back? Do you want her to? Is Lex going to become more interesting? What made the ghost start killing people out of the blue one day? What are those ghost doing down in the City all day?<br /><br />Self, you simply do not have enough to go on yet. Read book 3 and see what happens. It could become a deep and lasting love or go straight to hell. You have dated worse and survived. You know you want to. At least stay until you get screwed by a cliffhanger.</span>
