<div id="review_118451110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118451110" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118451110?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-jan-2012">zzread-jan-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118451110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7619246099714849044">Nobody writes dark urban fantasy like Stacia Kane. The author creates a world where ghosts wreak havoc and people turn to the Church to protect them. The Church provides people specially trained to get rid of ghosts. This is a world where summoning a ghost results in the death penalty. Ghosts kill and steal energy. <br/><br/>Part of the allure of this series is the way that the characters are written. Almost every character is flawed and yet, the reader feels invested in that character’s well-being. The m</span>
  <span id="freeText7619246099714849044" style="display:none">Nobody writes dark urban fantasy like Stacia Kane. The author creates a world where ghosts wreak havoc and people turn to the Church to protect them. The Church provides people specially trained to get rid of ghosts. This is a world where summoning a ghost results in the death penalty. Ghosts kill and steal energy. <br /><br />Part of the allure of this series is the way that the characters are written. Almost every character is flawed and yet, the reader feels invested in that character’s well-being. The main character Chess Putnam is a Church debunker or Church witch. Chess has a serious drug dependency problem – she is often strung out on a combination of pills. Even though she is an addict, Chess is surprisingly lucid, very good at her job, and able to research and solve her cases.<br /><br />Speaking of characters, this series has one of my favorite scary enforcers named Terrible. Oh, Terrible. If I saw you out in the streets, I would run in the opposite direction. Terrible is huge and not very attractive. The way he is written, the way he speaks, makes the reader see him in a different life. You want him to have a happy ending. He deserves it. <br /><br />In this book, we learn more about Chess’ past. We learn why she is so damaged and why she has become so drug dependent. Chess’ past gives us a clue why Chess cannot understand that someone could love her.<br /><br />There is a kind of love triangle going on. Stick with the books, the triangle is a function of Chess’ lack of self-respect rather than stringing on two men at a time. <br /><br />I can’t write a review about this book or this series without mentioning Downspeak the slang/patios used by residents of Downside. It adds a realistic touch to the chatter, dig? <br /><br />This series is not for everyone. It is most definitely an adult series, with adult situations and themes. If you like dark, urban fantasy, it is one of the better series out there. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7619246099714849044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144601388" />
    <a title="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines"><img alt="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405087473p2/4250664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144601388?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" href="/user/show/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines">Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144601388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3028268130501058629"><i>"Somewhere in the back of her mind she thought if she kept kissing him, she'd get more secrets, get answers to questions she didn't know she had, and it excited and scared her in equal measure, made her dizzy."</i> <br/><br/>I loved this book! I love living in Chess's (and Terrible's) world! <br/><br/>It's a little surprising the direction that Kane is taking this character in. Instead of showing her improving and battling her addiction, her situation seems to be drastically declining. I was able to grasp a better unde</span>
  <span id="freeText3028268130501058629" style="display:none"><i>"Somewhere in the back of her mind she thought if she kept kissing him, she'd get more secrets, get answers to questions she didn't know she had, and it excited and scared her in equal measure, made her dizzy."</i> <br><br>I loved this book! I love living in Chess's (and Terrible's) world! <br><br>It's a little surprising the direction that Kane is taking this character in. Instead of showing her improving and battling her addiction, her situation seems to be drastically declining. I was able to grasp a better understanding of just how bad off Chess really is. She describes things like her old, faded clothing and her blanket that is covered in holes because she spends every bit of her money on drugs. It's pretty pathetic. One half of me adores Chess and wants to see her overcome her addiction, but the other half of me doesn't want her to change because she's so damn interesting the way that she is.<br><br>At one point in the story you get to experience what happens to Chess when she has to spend one night without a fix. I had considered that maybe it would lead to a start on the road to recovery, but I was mistaken. Even with her many, many flaws Chess is too fascinating for me to dislike. The residents of Downside and the crazed, murderous ghosts that she encounters are equally as fascinating.<br><br> I can easily see how this series wouldn't be liked by everyone. Most people don't want to read about a poor, damaged, drug addicted, protagonist who shows no signs of advancing toward self-improvement, but regardless this is definitely one of my favorite series. <br><br>I've got City of Ghosts ordered and I hope it arrives soon!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380344891i/699703.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=best-book-boyfriend">best-book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=my-heart">my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=best-character-development">best-character-development</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2384224996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15827850504319625589">I believe I have found myself a new series to add to my all time favourite shelf.<br/><br/>But at the same time I don't really think this series is for everyone. I have also mentioned this before that this is a very complex book with very complex characters. It requires understanding and patience from readers, it's dark and sick and contains too many slangs. But there isn't a single thing about this book that I would ever want to change. <br/><br/>There are a few other things as well that might not appeal to other </span>
  <span id="freeText15827850504319625589" style="display:none">I believe I have found myself a new series to add to my all time favourite shelf.<br /><br />But at the same time I don't really think this series is for everyone. I have also mentioned this before that this is a very complex book with very complex characters. It requires understanding and patience from readers, it's dark and sick and contains too many slangs. But there isn't a single thing about this book that I would ever want to change. <br /><br />There are a few other things as well that might not appeal to other readers.<br /><br />Let's see.<br /><br />We all want to be able fall in love with the main character. Its highly important in order to keep moving forward with a book. We all love a badass, smart, strong headed heroine. <br /><br />Now let's talk about Chess here a bit. She is a lying bitch who all happens to a complete drug addict. She makes completely pathetic choices, ends up hurting people unintentionally and then goes and get high a little more. And then she will go make some stupid decision again. Sometimes with her you don't even know whom to kill – her or yourself. <br /><br />Sounds even worse than Bella or Anastasia huh?<br /><br />Personally, if someone ever gave me a character to read about with the traits mentioned above, I'd probably end up clawing my eyes out. So how is it possible that I managed to fall in love with Chess. You see, it’s how the book's written. Stacia Kane has somehow managed to paint Chess as such a powerful character, you will overlook so many things about her. <br /><br />Yes, Chess is a complete mess. Yes, she makes ridiculous choices at times but she isn't weak. Drugs are her weakness. Her addition makes her weak. But she is a strong character who has been through so much shit. In the previous book, we just got to peek a little into Chess’ soul. This book we get to see it raw and naked. We see her in her most vulnerable and helpless moments. This book made me feel for her, understand her in ways more than one. Her flaws didn't ever make me want to hurl the book out of the window like it should have. Instead she made me want to read more and more about her. <br /><br />Then we have Terrible. Another very very powerful character. In the last book we all fell in love with this ugly, huge and super scary man. But in this book, he will hit you like a truck. <br /><br />He is probably the best male MC I have ever read about in the whole Urban Fantasy universe. Despite him being described as ugly he manages to be so so so attractive. He's always respected Chess, never judged her and accepted her for who she was. He was scary to the world but so sweet to her. <br />Until she messes up. Big time. And then things become not so pretty between them. I am so glad we go to see this side of Terrible as well. I felt bad for Chess but I knew she deserved it. <i> She </i> knew she deserved it.<br />This was an important milestone in their relationship and it’s evolution. And I enjoyed every damned second of it.<br /><br />Moving onto the love triangle which in my opinion isn't much of a love triangle. And never was. From the start we knew Lex and Chess were just in a no string attached relationship. There wasn't much depth between their exchanges. Still isn't. Doesn't mean Lex isn't a great character. I have loved him from the start. He is funny and charming and not to mention extremely hot. What's not to like huh? <br /><br />Apart from the characters, the plot was really good – strong and gripping. At the same time, also dark, sick and creepy as hell. The pace was perfect and so was the writing. <br /><br />I would again like to appreciate Stacia Kane for what she has created here. Especially the downside speech – the broken English almost everyone in the Downside except for Chess had. It's always so fun reading it, especially when it comes from Terrible. It might seem easy to write broken English like that but when you notice certain expressions in those sentences you relalise being able to maintain that sort of dialect and all those slangs in it is an art in itself.<br /><br /> I would really really urge everyone to try this series. I can't guarantee everyone the same lovey dovey feeling towards it after but it's definitely worth a try :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15827850504319625589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5424751579731104362">Holy. Hell. <br/><br/>Wow.<br/><br/>I’m warning you now. This is going to be a really crappy review. It’s going to be an I-love-Kane/will-you-marry-me-Terrible kind of review. But can you blame a girl?<br/><br/>This book was so awesome. I am flying through this series and have only Stacia Kane to thank for this Terrible Fever I am in. <br/><br/>There are so many great things about this series. First off, I find that I love Church’s job. It gets her into some really messy situations, but I’m always interested in what is going on. Typic</span>
  <span id="freeText5424751579731104362" style="display:none">Holy. Hell. <br /><br />Wow.<br /><br />I’m warning you now. This is going to be a really crappy review. It’s going to be an I-love-Kane/will-you-marry-me-Terrible kind of review. But can you blame a girl?<br /><br />This book was so awesome. I am flying through this series and have only Stacia Kane to thank for this Terrible Fever I am in. <br /><br />There are so many great things about this series. First off, I find that I love Church’s job. It gets her into some really messy situations, but I’m always interested in what is going on. Typically with other UFs, I feel like their “ass-kicking job” is used as a filler, to bring some action in while the real story arc gains some meat. But in this series, I’m genuinely interested and find myself reading and rereading some of those parts. In this book, Chess has a celebrity assignment that brings her to the door of a rich but troubled family. As she works out the mystery concerning this family, Kane reveals a few secrets that had me gobsmacked.<br /><br />Another great thing about this series is the world. Downside has some pretty crazy and shitty things happen in it. But for some reason, I cannot get enough of it. It’s almost like a drug. I can’t stop wanting more.<br /><br />But perhaps the best thing about this series is TERRIBLE. I didn’t expect the romance subplot to take such an alarming twist in this book. The graveyard scene broke my heart and all the events following that only made me want to read the next book quicker. Chess makes a mistake. And now she is living with the consequence of that decision.<br /> <br />What I love is that Terrible kind of snuck up on me. I didn’t think I would grow to love him so hard, but I really, really do. I wish more authors wrote more characters like Terrible. We don’t see enough of these guys.<br /><br />Downside Ghosts has gone straight to the top of one of my favorite UF series EVER. And I know it only gets better. Come on Kane, gimme my next hit!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14955647397689674125">Unholy Magic is book two in the Downside Ghosts series & without a doubt my favorite new series of 2010. I have never in my life felt the need to email an author & wax poetic about how much I enjoyed their book until I read Unholy Magic!<br/><br/>I am a huge fan of Unholy Ghosts but I feel with Unholy Magicyou get to know Chess better, you already know what she’s about in the most basic of senses. We know Chess is a debunker as well as a drug addict, but we don’t really know why she is either. In Unholy M</span>
  <span id="freeText14955647397689674125" style="display:none">Unholy Magic is book two in the Downside Ghosts series &amp; without a doubt my favorite new series of 2010. I have never in my life felt the need to email an author &amp; wax poetic about how much I enjoyed their book until I read Unholy Magic!<br /><br />I am a huge fan of Unholy Ghosts but I feel with Unholy Magicyou get to know Chess better, you already know what she’s about in the most basic of senses. We know Chess is a debunker as well as a drug addict, but we don’t really know why she is either. In Unholy Magicyou get a little idea as to why Chess is the way she is, why she is addicted to drugs &amp; her life before she became a debunker. It’s not pretty, but it makes Chess, Chess. It was just more in depth in my opinion, you already know some of the back story from the previous book but now you’re learning what makes everyone tick. You understand the downspeak &amp; are comfortable with the world that Kane has written.<br /><br />The story is fabulous, Chess is working at a Celebrities house because he claims to have seen ghosts &amp; his wife was attacked by one of them. On top of that, there are hookers being murdered in a gruesome fashion &amp; no one has any idea why. We also get more into Chess relationship with Terrible &amp; Lex, trust me I wanted to strangle Chess at one point. There is also a HUGE epic moment towards the end of the book that had be going “WTF, OMG”, so book three in the series is going to be all sorts of drama I am sure. I will even admit that I cried. Uh-huh.<br /><br />I tried real hard to read Unholy Magic slowly, because the wait for City of Ghosts may be too much for me. I think I’m already going into withdrawals. Stacia Kane does not disappoint &amp; crafts one of the most original new series of 2010.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368518366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer851249743337248053">Unholy Magic is the 2nd in the Downside Ghosts series and boy, is it emotionally gripping and extremely intense. <br/><br/>Chess is a debunker for the Church who exterminates ghosts and more frequently, busts those who are set up fake hauntings for financial gain. She's also an extremely drug dependent, which helps her deal with the scars that early life experiences have caused. <br/><br/>In this book, we see her making horrible decisions that lead her to drive a divide between her personal relationships and the on</span>
  <span id="freeText851249743337248053" style="display:none">Unholy Magic is the 2nd in the Downside Ghosts series and boy, is it emotionally gripping and extremely intense. <br /><br />Chess is a debunker for the Church who exterminates ghosts and more frequently, busts those who are set up fake hauntings for financial gain. She's also an extremely drug dependent, which helps her deal with the scars that early life experiences have caused. <br /><br />In this book, we see her making horrible decisions that lead her to drive a divide between her personal relationships and the only person she really cares about, Terrible. Somehow, she's found herself wedged in between two opposing gang members, Terrible and Lex. It's evident throughout the book that she doesn't know how to deal when she actually cares about someone. <br /><br />Chess is such an interesting, complex character. We find out the reasons why she is so dependent on drugs and see her hit rock bottom in this book. Somehow, you just can't help but sympathise with her and wish that she will one day find solace in something that isn't drugs. Stacia Kane has a way with conveying heavy emotions throughout the book. This is not an easy read, with so many dark themes involving sex, drugs, and murder. <br /><br />The world of Downside is so corrupt, dark and gritty. The crimes performed within this book are not for the squeamish, involving mutilated bodies, necrophilia, and the like. Once you become adjusted to the world of Downside, you'll be in for a heck of a ride as you follow Chess on her journey of debunking and ghost-busting.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out Happy Indulgence for more reviews!</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1193741293" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1193741293" />
    <a title="Tanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31718503-tanya"><img alt="Tanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401904331p2/31718503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4531338-mrs-vishous-kattalakis-belikov-para-itch-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164705944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11468400174047948714">This series is one of the greatest!! Its like being sucked in to a whole new world thats dark and scary and full of the unknown. I didnt think I would like a book about the protaganist being an addict with no dreams of recovery....but it worked and I wouldnt have it any other way! One of the sweetest moments in literary history:<br/><br/><i>"I figure you really wanted me you'd say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I'll fuckin carry you down your place on a run, you tell me aye, get you on your back afore the nex</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11468400174047948714" style="display:none">This series is one of the greatest!! Its like being sucked in to a whole new world thats dark and scary and full of the unknown. I didnt think I would like a book about the protaganist being an addict with no dreams of recovery....but it worked and I wouldnt have it any other way! One of the sweetest moments in literary history:<br /><br /><i>"I figure you really wanted me you'd say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I'll fuckin carry you down your place on a run, you tell me aye, get you on your back afore the next word comes out your mouth. But you oughta have yourself certain, causen I ain't lookin for charity, an I ain't lettin you go after. Once...once ain't enough for me, dig?"</i><br /><br />I really thought she was learning her lesson and admitting to herself that she really wanted to be with him....Especially when Terrible came to her rescue at the Pyles'.(I must say that her withdrawal was the most powerful scenes Iv ever read.)<br />Then this idiot was to damn scared to take the fecking leap when he basically confessed his love to her...I was soooo disappointed in Chess at that moment! She really fucked herself over with this love triangle she had going on! And it was so sad when Terrible busted her...at the same time....Im glad her dumb ass got caught. She really pissed me off with that one. She knew how Terrible felt about her and she went ahead and fucked Lex anyway! She shouldnt even been in that graveyard with him in the first place.<br /><br /><i>"Two nights past. He say two nights past, aye? Two nights---you seen him? That night you seen him, after I--you went from--"</i><br /><br />Then to top it all off <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I thought Terrible was dead! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Thank God he wasnt. I swear I was about to be real Feckin Pissed and loose all hope in UF!! That said....this series is one wild fecking ride!</span>

<div id="review_258695341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258695341" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258695341?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258695341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11843624585090818544">I guess it says alot about this book that it has inspired such a tangled mess of emotions in me. I'm angry at Chess. I feel sorry for her. I feel like she deserves her misery, but I want it to all work out. Her self-destructive behavior doesn't just affect her, but the fallout is landing on those around her. --And I'm getting ahead of myself.<br/><br/>Three months have passed since the events of <i>Unholy Ghosts</i>. Chess is still a raging drug addict. She is still sleeping with Lex. And she is still forging a </span>
  <span id="freeText11843624585090818544" style="display:none">I guess it says alot about this book that it has inspired such a tangled mess of emotions in me. I'm angry at Chess. I feel sorry for her. I feel like she deserves her misery, but I want it to all work out. Her self-destructive behavior doesn't just affect her, but the fallout is landing on those around her. --And I'm getting ahead of myself.<br /><br />Three months have passed since the events of <i>Unholy Ghosts</i>. Chess is still a raging drug addict. She is still sleeping with Lex. And she is still forging a friendship with Terrible. Only she can't see that it's really something more.<br /><br />Her latest job for the church is to try and debunk the supposed haunting of a famous actor's home. Meanwhile, her latest mission on the street is to figure out who is using a ghost to help them kill off Downside's prostitutes and gouge their eyes out. Once again, I am amazed to find Chess surviving it all, considering her incredibly bad choices and divided loyalties.<br /><br />But obviously, I am not feeling too charitable towards her right now. I guess that's because Terrible has stolen a piece of my heart. The man is far, far too good for her. She proves it over and over. And yet, I want them to work things out so badly, it's like an anvil on my chest. ((**sigh**))<br /><br />I guess you can say I have grown invested in the series. It's still kind of strange. But I'm getting used to it. Stacia Kane has created a world like no other I've read about. And her characters, while flawed, are very compelling. A powerful and unexpected ending that has me itching to find out what happens next. 4 1/2 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11843624585090818544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4257355906831493742">2-2.5 stars<br/><br/>God, this book...actually, the first TWO books in this series, are so damn depressing. <br/><br/>This took me a long time to finish. I kept having to take breaks from it because the entire thing is just so...bleak. There were certain parts that were very hard for me to read (I.e Chess going through withdrawals), and there were times when I nearly gave up on the book. But, my love for Trouble, and the fact that I do find the whole Downside world...and DownSpeak...to be so fascinating most of the</span>
  <span id="freeText4257355906831493742" style="display:none">2-2.5 stars<br /><br />God, this book...actually, the first TWO books in this series, are so damn depressing. <br /><br />This took me a long time to finish. I kept having to take breaks from it because the entire thing is just so...bleak. There were certain parts that were very hard for me to read (I.e Chess going through withdrawals), and there were times when I nearly gave up on the book. But, my love for Trouble, and the fact that I do find the whole Downside world...and DownSpeak...to be so fascinating most of the time, was what kept me reading. <br /><br />I will say that Chess' self destructive behavior and self hatred is really hard for me to handle at times. It makes sense...to a certain degree...in that world and considering her life, but still, it's not something I enjoy reading about.</span>

<div id="review_251337150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251337150" />
    <a title="Emmy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5100450-emmy"><img alt="Emmy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429946409p2/5100450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251337150?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emmy" href="/user/show/5100450-emmy">Emmy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5100450-emmy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251337150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8551653813884472791">Uh, yeah. There might be spoilers here. And I write this while listening to the Stooges. That seems appropriate.<br/><br/><br/><br/>So this was my favorite book out of the 3 out so far. The plot is crazy. There are dead prostitutes with missing eyeballs. This brings together both sides (and I'm not talking the Church) working with Chess to put a stop to it. The other storyline is her debunking a case for an actor and his family which leads to such an emotional and horrible scene with Chess going through withdrawal.</span>
  <span id="freeText8551653813884472791" style="display:none">Uh, yeah. There might be spoilers here. And I write this while listening to the Stooges. That seems appropriate.<br /><br /><br /><br />So this was my favorite book out of the 3 out so far. The plot is crazy. There are dead prostitutes with missing eyeballs. This brings together both sides (and I'm not talking the Church) working with Chess to put a stop to it. The other storyline is her debunking a case for an actor and his family which leads to such an emotional and horrible scene with Chess going through withdrawal. That was insanely intense. <br /><br />So lets get to some quotes from the books:<br /><br /><b>“Think we help each other here, ain’t you? Got anything I can help you with, Tulip?” <br />“Maybe.” She reached back, finding him hard and ready beneath his jeans and opening them. <br />He made a low, satisfied sound in the back of his throat, one she’d come to associate with him and the time they spent in his bed. The cigarette flew into the sink and landed with a tiny sizzle. His palms slid up her ribcage under her shirt, under her bra, then back down to shove her jeans and panties off her hips. <br />“What you say? Gonna help me? Come round my neighborhood, check the sights?” His hand on the back of her neck forced her gently down, bending her over the counter, while one knee pressed the inside of her thigh and urged her legs apart as far as they could go with her jeans pooled around her ankles. His erection butted up against her, hovering, waiting. “Sure could use you, Tulip.”</b><br /><br />~ So this is Lex and Chess. I like Lex but can't forget that yes, he did kidnap her to take advantage of her. But they do have their sizzling moments. I still think he cares but business is business. He just happens to mix business with pleasure.<br /><br />And that brings me to the scene on the rooftop. Damn. Just, damn. <br /><b>“Shit. I want you, Chess. Make no mistake on that one, dig? Want you bad. So bad I ain’t even can think of any else sometimes, ’cept gettin you under me. Ain’t give a fuck what pills you swallow get you through the day or what happens you ain’t got em, aye? Still want you.”<br />...<br />I ain’t … ain’t think I can take it, wakin up next to you on the morn, have you fake like nothin happened. Or tell me you made yourself a mistake. Or say, aye, thanks, maybe try that again on the sometime. I know how you run it, keepin it cool and no repeats, and I dig it, aye? Got your reasons. So I figure …”<br />...<br />“I figure you really wanted me you’d say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I’ll fuckin carry you down your place on a run, you tell me aye, get you on your back afore the next word out your mouth. But you oughta have yourself certain, causen I ain’t lookin for charity, an I ain’t lettin you go after. Once … once ain’t enough for me, dig?”</b><br />~ Such raw emotion from Terrible. It was painful to read and my heart broke for him but I'm happy he let his true feelings out. <br /><br />But then what happens at the cemetery? I can't... I can't describe my thoughts on that. As I mentioned in my review of <i>Unholy Ghosts</i>, Chess makes mistakes and this reveals her biggest one. Her running to Lex. I can't formulate words to describe how much I feel for Terrible when he realizes. I just want to hug him.<br /><br />But then Terrible makes some harsh comments to her when she is putting sigils on his face and I can't blame the guy. I really can't. I don't think Chess knew what she was doing at the time but she still did it. Yes, her relationship with Lex started before she really admitted to herself she had any feelings for Terrible, but still. She runs to Lex's place after what happened at Chuck's in book 1 with Terrible and now she runs to Lex again after what happens on the roof. <br /><br />Then the ending happens. He put himself in danger to save her, and she completely cracks. I would have felt really awkward if I was Lex after watching her break down.<br /><br />This is my favorite book so far. So much happens. Many ups and downs. I think she really has some life changing experiences though that help her see what she is lying to herself about. <br /><br />I love this book. I love this series and just barely finished but want to do an immediate re-read. 5 stars all the way.<br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8551653813884472791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128083666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128083666" />
    <a title="Francesca the Fierce (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Francesca the Fierce (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595947372p2/3108364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128083666?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Francesca the Fierce (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Francesca the Fierce (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog">Francesca the Fierce (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-read-2011">books-read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=ghost-spirit-necromancer">ghost-spirit-necromancer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-urban-fantasy">genre-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3108364-francesca-the-fierce-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-audio-books">read-audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128083666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13953931403001105351">This review was posted at <a href='http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/09/review-unholy-magic-by-stacia-kane.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under The Covers</a><br/><br/>After reading book one, and being shocked by the storyline in this series, I find myself a lot more comfortable with Chess and her issues in this book. Don't ask me why. I get it. It didn't bother me as much.<br/><br/>Now that being said... Chess is a lot more vulnerable in this book. She is trying to do her job, which now consists in going to a celebrity's house to prove that he doesn't really have a ghost problem.<br/><br/>Well, that is her mission with the Church. But of</span>
  <span id="freeText13953931403001105351" style="display:none">This review was posted at <a href="http://underthecoversbookblog.blogspot.com/2011/09/review-unholy-magic-by-stacia-kane.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Under The Covers</a><br /><br />After reading book one, and being shocked by the storyline in this series, I find myself a lot more comfortable with Chess and her issues in this book. Don't ask me why. I get it. It didn't bother me as much.<br /><br />Now that being said... Chess is a lot more vulnerable in this book. She is trying to do her job, which now consists in going to a celebrity's house to prove that he doesn't really have a ghost problem.<br /><br />Well, that is her mission with the Church. But of course, she has to do side jobs for her "friends". Terrible asks her to investigate something going on at an abandoned airport. Lex on the other hand also has interests in that same investigation. So she ends up working for both behind both backs.<br /><br />And there in lays the problem. This book was a royal mess! A big fuck up. A WHAT THE HELL WAS SHE THINKING???? I mean, if the fact that she keeps getting high, especially when she's on the job, is not enough to make you think she's missing a few screws, then her actions in this book have made her certifiably nuts.<br /><br />Here is a wonderful guy, Terrible. Yeah, I know, he's ugly, he works for a drug dealer/pimp. Not your standard hero material. But I can't help but feel an attraction to him. It's in the way he cares for Chess. How he's always there for her, and would give his life (and almost does) for her. He can look pass her issues and see the good inside of her that she can't see herself. And what she does to him in this book, well, it simply puts her on my bad side. Yes, I cried. I wanted to scream at her! How could she do this? This is not going to be an easy fix.<br /><br />Can I bitch some more about that? Because it really got to me. Yeah? OK, how can you have a guy open up his heart and serve it on a platter for you the way he did, and you just stomp all over it. And tap dance on it. Damn! It just broke my heart.<br /><br />But at least Chess was on her game with her investigations! I loved the story! This series is dark and intense. Ms. Kane has created a very unique world an I'll be back for more!<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quote:</b><br /><br /><i>"But I ain't, I ain't think I can take it. Waking up next to you on the morn, have you fake like nothing happened. Or say, aight thanks, maybe we can try that again on the sometime. I know how you run it. Keepin' it cool and no repeats, and I dig it aight? Got your reasons. So I figured...I figured you'd really wanted me, you'd say. Like now, maybe, if you dig. I'll fucking carry you down to your place on a run if you tell me aight. Get you on your back before the next word comes out your mouth. But you oughta have yourself certain, 'cuz I ain't looking for charity, and I ain't letting you go after. Once? Once ain't enough for me. Dig?" </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13953931403001105351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_112256414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112256414" />
    <a title="Smokinhotbooks K.C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2841223-smokinhotbooks-k-c"><img alt="Smokinhotbooks K.C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255740001p2/2841223.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112256414?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smokinhotbooks K.C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smokinhotbooks K.C." href="/user/show/2841223-smokinhotbooks-k-c">Smokinhotbooks K.C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2841223-smokinhotbooks-k-c?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2841223-smokinhotbooks-k-c?shelf=uf">uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112256414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16393801067500412919"><a href='http://smokinhotbooks.com/blog/2010/07/19/unholyghosts/' rel='nofollow noopener'>(Combined review of Unholy Magic and Unholy Ghosts) </a><br/><br/>It’s not often that you will find me reading a book about a drug- addicted heroine who makes more terrible choices than Lindsey Lohan on a four day coke bender; but at the urging of my blogger friends I decided to stop being such a square and see what all the hoopla was about. As the rehab therapists would say, I had to “trust the process’.<br/><br/>Stacia Kane’s Downside Ghost series is dark, thrilling and gut wrenching. Chess Putnam works as the ‘Churc</span>
  <span id="freeText16393801067500412919" style="display:none"><a href="http://smokinhotbooks.com/blog/2010/07/19/unholyghosts/" rel="nofollow noopener">(Combined review of Unholy Magic and Unholy Ghosts) </a><br /><br />It’s not often that you will find me reading a book about a drug- addicted heroine who makes more terrible choices than Lindsey Lohan on a four day coke bender; but at the urging of my blogger friends I decided to stop being such a square and see what all the hoopla was about. As the rehab therapists would say, I had to “trust the process’.<br /><br />Stacia Kane’s Downside Ghost series is dark, thrilling and gut wrenching. Chess Putnam works as the ‘Churchwich’ for a new order Church that indoctrinates the motto “Facts Are Truth”. They employ debunkers who use magic to rid the world of murderous ghosts. The world is in a post-genocide era, where the dead have risen and attack the living. The government has fallen, and the Church of Truth is now in power …<br /><br />At first, I was worried that I would have a hard time connecting with Chess. Writing your main heroine as a drug addict whose life is spiraling dangerously out of control is an intricate balance. To create a sort of alternative, anti-hero who still has some redeeming qualities that allow her to appear vulnerable without playing the “Im a victim card” is the make of a truly talented writer. And that is the genius of Kane’s writing. She really makes the reader understand the depth of Chess ability to survive a life that most would turned in the keys and signed off. Abandoned and placed in foster care, her life is filled with one violation of trust after another. You truly understand that to forget the pain of the past, to live a somewhat ‘normal’ life you need something to numb the past. You don’t battle the demons without a few toxic coping mechanisms.<br /><br />I was so taken with how vibrant and alive Kane has made her characters. Her dark, urban setting was fascinating rather than graphic and I have fallen head over heels with Terrible. (The body-guard/bouncer for Chess drug-dealer of choice, Bump). The intensity of Chess and Terrible’s budding friendship shows that even the most hardened shell can be cracked with just a little kindness, a little compassion. Although, their relationship is tenuous at best, you can’t help but be captivated and root for them.<br /><br />Unholy Ghosts and Unholy Magic are two of the best books I’ve read of 2010 and 2009. I’m not going to lie, the second book will tear your heart out, you may even find yourself emotionally ‘stress eating’ but so worth it. I promise! This series has grit, angst, violence, and pulls you in with each page – if you haven’t read this series, get thee to a bookstore post haste!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16393801067500412919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XBVCLRZDRVTxGTO3GQ/UyxgjBslAB/z8dCDwxDCbIR8VsZPZdA0MwzpM4uzvIinKLIOkB9vvXJf6hPAFDJWHWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XapN1n3fr7PSJwvORRbL1P+rF81hrYDoXSCQ7gYN8YEUDpwiH5HmJBly2pWzOzbVywu1A/pFIIPThJAvOgNXxg==')})
  }
